+Jamison Brereton

13 (633)
Indra
N─Бrada K─Бс╣Зva
33 verses: uс╣гс╣Зih, arranged in trcas ╠е
Though, like the previous hymn (VIII.12), this one is in uс╣гс╣Зih meter and arranged in tr╠еcas, the tight structuring of VIII.12 is absent here, save in the final tr╠еca (vss. 31тАУ33) with its four-syllable refrain and repeated identifications with the тАЬbull,тАЭ and most of the tr╠еcas lack clear unity. The theme of growing and making strong found in VIII.12 is continued here, howeverтАФnotably in the first tr╠еca (vss. 1тАУ3) and that formed by verses 16тАУ18, but also generally throughout the hymn. There are also less insistent links between different parts of the hymn (e.g., the tree branches of vss. 6, 17), and some pleasing turns of phrase, like the тАЬsea of the stalkтАЭ (vs. 15) referring to a particular large vessel of soma.
Mythological material is mostly lacking in the hymn, and what is found is given perfunctory treatment (see the allusions to the Maruts in vss. 20 and 28тАУ29). The focus instead is the usual give-and-take of the ritual compact. Although the hymn has no spectacularly memorable features, it does not seem to deserve GeldnerтАЩs scornful dismissal as тАЬein recht nichtssagendes [тАШtrivialтАЩ or тАШvacuousтАЩ] Lied.тАЭ1054 VIII.13

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Indra Although the introduction. to the published translation is somewhat dismissive of this hymn and dubious about any unifying factors, closer examination shows a subsurface thematic unity esp. in the mid and later parts of the hymn, roughly vss. 16-30. For discussion see below.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬIndra, when the Soma juices are effused, sanctifies the offerer and the praiser for the attainment ofincrease giving strength, for he is mighty.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Sanctifies: kratum pun─лta ukthyam = karmaс╣З─Бm kart─Бramsto_t─Бram ca;

Ukthya = name of a sacrifice, ukthy─Бkhyam y─Бgam

+Jamison Brereton

When the soma juices have been pressed, Indra purifies his resolve, which is worthy of hymns.
He knows his own strengthening skill, for he is great.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

For b see VIII.12.11.

+Griffith

INDRA, when Soma juices flow, makes his mind pure and meet for lauds.
He gains the power that brings success, for great is he.

+Geldner

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬAbiding in the highest heaven, in the dwelling of the gods, he is the giver of increase, the accomplisher(of works), the possessor of great renown, the conqueror of (the obstructer of) the rains.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

In the first highest heaven, in the seat of the gods, he is the
strengthening one,
affording good passage, foremost in fame, entirely victorious amid the waters.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The word apsuj├нt never occurs without an immediately preceding s├бm, whose function is not clear. See VIII.36.1-6, IX.106.3. Dissatsifaction with this expression goes back to Ludwig, and Scarlatta (154-55) suggests that the phrase is a metrically more favorable version of *aps├║ s├бс╣Гjit тАЬcompletely victorious in the waters.тАЭ This has some merit, but itтАЩs also worth noting in this metrical context that there seems to be a feeling that a preverb is a good way to start the final four syllables of an Uс╣гс╣Зih, and when in doubt s├бm is a safe one. See in the previous hymn VIII.12.16-18 s├бm ├нndubhiс╕е (though the s├бm is functional there), 22-24 s├бm ├│jase, - aс╕е. In its other two occurrences (VIII.36.1-6, IX.106.3), s├бm apsuj├нt is a separable 4- syllable p─Бda (as long as one accepts OldenbergтАЩs analysis of the meter of VIII.36; see comm. there).

+Griffith

In heaven’s first region, in the seat of Gods, is he who brings success,
Most glorious, prompt to save, who wins the water-floods.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWhen your discriminating eulogist has addressed to you overpowering praises, then, if they areacceptable to you, they expand like the branches (of a tree).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Overpowering: i.e., able to overpower enemies,┼Ыatr┼лс╣З─Бm prahasanasamarth─Бс╕е

+Jamison Brereton

When the boundless praiser makes bold his songs for you,
your *vitality grows afterward as branches do, when they take pleasure.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

In c the subject of sg. rohate тАШgrowsтАЩ is apparently unexpressed. Geldner supplies Indra, while supplying the songs as subject of the pl. juс╣г├бnta, which he seems to take as transitive тАШpleaseтАЩ: тАЬdann w├дchst er [n. Indra] wie Zweige nach, wenn sie [n. Lobreden] wohlgefallen,тАЭ though I have trouble interpreting his tr. But forms of juс╣г├бte almost always mean тАШtake pleasureтАЩ, not тАШgive pleasureтАЩ (see 29b for juс╣г├бnta in just this sense). To tackle the latter problem first, I take the subject of juс╣г├бnta to be the closest plural noun, namely тАШbranchesтАЩ. Although the notion of branches enjoying themselves seems odd, I suggest it may refer to their growth under favorable conditions, with good soil and the proper amounts of water and light.

(Modern gardening manuals often say that a plant тАЬlikesтАЭ this or that condition.) As for the subject of rohate, I take it as an imperfect pun: the form vay─Б╠Б(с╕е) is, on the one hand, the nom. pl. of vay─Б╠Б- тАШbranchтАЩ; however, a *v├бya(с╕е), which would differ from the text only by accent and the length of the final vowel, could be the nom. sg. of the neut. -s-stem meaning тАШvitalityтАЩ, and so I take it. Alternatively one could follow BloomfieldтАЩs suggestion (made at the parallel passage II.5.4) that vay─Б╠Б(с╕е) is the masc.

nom. sg. of an internally derived *vay├бs- тАШpossessing vitality, vital oneтАЩ (=Indra). In fact I now prefer this solution and would change the published translation accordingly, to тАЬthe vital one growsтАЭ (though in this case we might expect a 2nd sg. verb). (In II.5.4 this is unnecessary because Agni is easily and properly supplied as subject, and the tree branches work fine in the simile.)

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬPraise the renowned, the sapient (Indra), whose victorious horses proceed to the dwelling of the devoutdonor (of the libation).тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

that go to the house of the pious and reverential man.

+Griffith

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬI invoke you when the sun is risen; I invoke (you) at mid-day; being propitited, come to us, Indra, withyour gliding steeds.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

I call upon you when the sun has risen; I call upon (you) at the dayтАЩs midday.
Rejoicing, Indra, come here to us with your teams.

+Griffith

I call thee when the Sun is risen, I call thee at the noon of day:
With thy car-horses, Indra, come wellpleased to us.

+Geldner

Ich rufe dich bei Sonnenaufgang, ich rufe dich um die Mittagszeit des Tages; komm gern zu uns, Indra, mit deinen Gespannen!

+Grassmann

Dich ruf’ bei Sonnenaufgang ich, dich in des Tages Mitte an; Mit den Gespannen komme froh, o Indra, her.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬCome quickly; hasten, be exhilarated by the libation mixed with milk; extend the ancient sacrifice, sothat I may obtain (its reward).тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Come here! Run forth! Take the exhilaration of the pressed (soma) accompanied by cows.
Stretch the ancient thread in the way that is known.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Although Geldner interprets the stretching of the thread as a metaphorical expression for the continuation of old relationships, it seems far more likely that it reflects the normal idiom тАЬstretch the threadтАЭ for setting up and performing the sacrifice. See vs. 18b dev─Б╠Бso yaj├▒├бm atnata. тАЬThe way that is knownтАЭ means the standard procedure. That Indra is being urged to do this, rather than the sacrificers, might be a little odd, but see, in fact, 18b just cited, as well as 30c m├нm─лte yaj├▒├бm.

+Griffith

Speed forward hither, come to us, rejoice thee in the milky draught:
Spin out the thread of ancient time, as well is known.

+Geldner

Komm doch her, beeile dich doch, berausche dich am milchgemischten Soma, spann den altgewohnten Faden, wie bekannt!

+Grassmann

O komm doch her, o eile doch, und trink vom milchgemischten Saft; Den alten Faden webe fort nach deiner Art.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe pious, desiring his protection, magnify him by ample and plural asure- yielding (libations); the earth,(and other worlds, spread out) like the branches of a tree, magnify Indra.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Just him did the inspired poets, seeking aid, (increase) with downward coursing help.
The battle cries made Indra increase, as tree-branches do.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

I am puzzled as to what тАЬdownward coursing help(s)тАЭ (prav├бtvat─лbhir ┼лt├нbhiс╕е) might be. As Geldner points out, vs. 25 shows that the instr. phrase should be construed with avardhayan and so it must be help that the poets are giving Indra rather than getting from him (though they themselves are also avasy├бvaс╕е тАШseeking aidтАЩ). The stem prav├бtvant- is generally used of landscape/cosmic features that have a gentle, and by implication pleasant and easily traversed, slope; see esp. V.54.9, where heaven and earth, the paths, and the mountains all provide a prav├бt- for the MarutsтАЩ journey. The help provided to Indra by the poets may be of the same quality, smoothing and easing his journey to the sacrifice and his participation in it. In our 8b we met waters at play going along a slope (prav├бt─Б). Again тАШdownhill, sloping downтАЩ implies the path of least resistance and the opposite of effortful activity. If the identification of the poets with the Maruts suggested above is correct, it might be worth noting that four of the seven forms of prav├бtvant- are found in a single verse in a Marut hymn (the aforementioned V.54.9).

We meet vay─Б╠Бiva again, repeating the simile of 6c. As in 6 I think that the tree branches are compared with Indra (and hence are acc. here), rather than being compared to the battle cries. They make Indra grow as tree-branches grow.

+Griffith

Him sages longing for his aid, with offerings brought in eager haste,
Him. even as branches, all mankind have made to grow.

+Geldner

Denselben machten die beistandsuchenden Barden, den Indra sein Gefolge mit raschen Hilfen gro├Я wie die Zweige den Baum.

+Grassmann

Gunst suchend liessen wachsen ihn die Priester durch der Opfer Strom, Den Indra der Gew├дsser Flut wie Zweige ihn.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe progeny of Rudra (the Maruts) is known in ancient plural ces, and to them the intelligent worshippersoffer adoration.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

He perceives just that youthful (troop) of Rudra [=Maruts] in the ancient domains,
where the discerning ones [=Maruts?] have distributed that thought.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

This verse is quite opaque and its grammar can be construed in a number of different ways, giving the lie to GeldnerтАЩs breezy тАЬDie Konstruktion ist klar.тАЭ See OldenbergтАЩs rather more despairing assessment (тАЬEs ergeben sich mannigfache M├╢glichkeiten, zwischen denen sichere Entscheidung ausgeschlossenтАжтАЭ).

The first problem is the value of the verb cetati and, when that has been determined, the identity of its subject. Geldner takes the verb as intransitive/reflexive тАЬтАж zeichnet sich тАж aus,тАЭ but an I/T value (тАШperceiveтАЩ) is also possible for this active stem. I interpret it so (as does Oldenberg in one of his suggested tr.), and continue as its subject the stot─Б╠Бof vs. 19.

The next issue is the reference and distribution of t├бd ├нd rudr├бsya тАж yahv├бm, which Geldner takes as subject of cetati and I as object. I will not rehearse the various suggested possibilities (see Geldner and Oldenberg), but simply add my own: rudr├бsya is generally used with ‘son(s)’ to refer to the Maruts, who can be called ‘young’ in that context (cf. V.42.15b rudr├бsya s┼лn┼л╠Бm╠Рr yuvany┼л╠Бn…); and a neut. noun regularly used for the Maruts is ┼Ы├бrdhas- тАШtroopтАЩ, as in the nearby hymn VIII.15.9c ┼Ы├бrdhaс╕е тАж m─Б╠Бrutam. In fact see m─Б╠Бrutaс╣Г ┼Ы├бrdhaс╕е in the p─Бda immediately preceding V.42.15b, namely 15a, where the singular (15a) and plural (15b) expressions are coreferential.

So here I supply that noun with t├бd тАж yahv├бm.

Then what are the тАЬancient domainsтАЭ? On the basis of IX.52.2 pratn├йbhir ├бdhvabhiс╕е тАЬalong your age-old routes,тАЭ referring to the protocols of the soma sacrifice and the ritual journey of soma, I suggest that the ancient domains here are the age-old practices of the sacrifice. It is essentially equivalent to 14c t├бntuс╣Г tanuс╣гva p┼лrvy├бс╣Г y├бth─Б vid├й тАЬStretch the ancient thread in the way that is known.тАЭ In c I take v├нcetasaс╕е to refer again to the Maruts. For the switch between singular and plural see V.42.15 just cited. The Maruts are called v├нcetas- in V.54.13.

What the whole verse means and what function it fills in the hymn are not clear to me. If my interpretation of the various parts is correct (and I have no confidence that it is), the successful human praiser of vs. 19 perceives his divine model, the Maruts, whose praise inspired Indra in the Vс╣Ыtra battle, at his sacrifice, where they have placed the thought or mental power that he should himself follow.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬIf, (Indra), you choose my friendship, partake of this (sacrificial) food, by which we may pass beyond(the reach of) all adversaries.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

If you will choose my companionship, drink of this stalk,
by which we have crossed beyond all hatreds.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

I struggle to make the final verse of the tс╣Ыca fit with the speculative scenario sketched for the first two verses (19-20). (As far as I can tell, neither Geldner nor Oldenberg makes the attempt, an omission with which I am in sympathy.) One thing to account for is the switch from 3rd ps. in 19-20 (though note te in 19a) to a 1st

-2nd partnership in 21. I suggest that the stot─Б╠Бin 19 (and 20, by my reading) is now the 1st ps. speaker of 21. He offers Indra companionship or partnership (sakhy├бm) modeled on that shared by Indra and the Maruts, of which he had a vision in vs. 20. The sign of IndraтАЩs chosing his companionship will be his (=IndraтАЩs) acceptance of the speakerтАЩs offered soma.

On ─Б╠Бv├бraс╕е see comm. on I.143.6. It may be better to tr. it as тАШgrantтАЩ, rather than тАШchooseтАЩ. If so, I would change the sentence immediately above to тАЬThe sign of IndraтАЩs granting his companionship тАжтАЭ

+Grassmann

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWhen, Indra, who delight in praise, may your worshipper be entirely happy? When will you establish usin (the affluence of) cattle, of horses, of dwellings?тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

O Indra who longs for songs, when will your praiser become most wealful for you?
When will you place us amid bovine and equine goods?

+Jamison Brereton Notes

One piece of evidence for my interpretation of the preceding tс╣Ыca as having the praiser (stot├бr-) as its thematic center is his reappearance in this verse, in this anxious question. The verse expresses the reciprocity inherent in the ritual situation, with the praiser wishing to be тАЬmost wealfulтАЭ for Indra, while also receiving his own benefits from the god. This reminds us of verse 17, where the poets (quite possibly the Maruts) were both seeking help and making Indra increase through the help they gave him.

+Griffith

When wilt thou grant us wealth in herds of kine and steeds?

+Geldner

Wann wird dir, lobbegehrender Indra, der S├дnger am meisten zusagen? Wann wirst du uns zu Rinder- und Rossebesitz, zu Gut verhelfen?

+Grassmann

Wann wird, o Indra, Liederfreund, der S├дnger dir am liebsten sein? Wann wirst du Gut an Rind und Ross uns hold verleihn?

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬPraised of many, prosper (us) with the protections hymned by the с╣Ыс╣гis, send down upon us nutritiousfood.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Become increased, o you who are praised by many, with your forms of help that are praised by the seers.
Milk out swelling refreshment, and help us.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

This verse both parrots the preceding verse (24ab тАж puruс╣гс╣нut╚зm, тАж ┼лt├нbhiс╕е / 25ab тАж puruс╣гс╣нuta, тАж ┼лt├нbhiс╕е) and concentrates into a single expression the reciprocal aid between god and praiser that has dominated the rhetoric of the last tс╣Ыcas. In the command vardhasva тАж ┼лt├нbhiс╕е тАЬbecome increased тАж by forms of help,тАЭ the instr. should express the means by which Indra becomes strong, and that should be the help given him by others, as in vs. 17 t├бm ├нd v├нpr─Бс╕е тАж ┼лt├нbhiс╕е / тАж avardhayanтАж тАЬThe inspired poets increased him with helps.тАЭ But the forms of help in 25 are с╣Ы╠Бс╣гistut─Бbhiс╕е тАШpraised by the seersтАЩ, which suggests that these are forms of help given by Indra to us, like those in 24b. The condensed expression in this verse sets up a closed circle, a never-ending loop, in which forms of help given and received are identical and have identical results. With that established, the poet then presses his advantage and in p─Бda c and in 26a puts Indra squarely in the role of helping us.

Pour down for us abundant food and guard us well.

Although Geldner gives up on the cmpd. prat├бdvas┼л, which modifies h├бr─л, Oldenberg plausibly suggests that itтАЩs a univerbation of the frequent collocation pr├б t├бd тАЬforth to thatтАЭ or perhaps pr├б t├бd v├бsu тАЬforth to that good thing,тАЭ perhaps as the actual command Indra тАЬcries outтАЭ to the horses. +Wilson
English translation:

тАЬMay the sons of Rudra, who are your followers, approach and partake of the glory (of the sacrifice); andmay (other celestial) people associated with the Maruts (partake of the sacrificial) food.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Glory: ┼Ыriyam =┼Ыrayaс╣З─лyam yaj├▒am

+Jamison Brereton

Let them cry outтАФthose who are yours: the Rudras accompany your splendor,
as do the clans of Maruts, to your satisfaction.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Note the chaining over tс╣Ыca boundary: 27c тАж abh├н svara# / 28a #abh├н svarantu.

Most interpreters (Geldner, Oldenberg, Klein [I.383]) take sakс╣гata as the verb of the relative clause beginning y├й t├бva, but it is unaccented. Oldenberg recognizes the problem but considers it unnatural to separate t├бva from ┼Ыr├нyam and accounts for the lack of accent acdg to ZDMG 60, 737-38 [=Kl.Sch. 212-13], namely occasional lack of accent when the rel. pronoun and the verb are in different p─Бdas (not, in my opinion, a compelling explanation in any of these cases). But y├й t├бva functions fine as an independent rel. clause, and supplying тАШyourтАЩ again with ┼Ыr├нyam is no problem in an independent clause.

Geldner supplies тАЬcomeтАЭ in c, but the verb in b can do duty here as well.

The Maruts, who were only latent in vs. 20 (and probably 17), appear here with Rudra, who was present in vs. 20. The Marut clans here may pick up the clans in 16c; see above.

+Griffith

Attendants on thy glory, let the Rudras roar assent to thee,
And all the Marut companies come to the feast.

+Geldner

Die Rudras├╢hne, die deine Herrlichkeit begleiten, sollen einstimmen. Auch die marutischen Clane kommen zum Opferschmaus.

+Grassmann

Her rausche auch die Rudraschar, begleitend deine sch├╢ne Pracht, Die Marutst├дmme allzumal zum Labetrunk.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬMay those who (are his attndants), victorious (over enemies), be satisfied with the station (which theyoccupy) in heaven, and may they be assembled at the navel of the sacrifice, that I may therefrom acquire(wealth).тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

These (clans), his advance (troops), find pleasure in the track that is in heaven.
In the navel of the sacrifice they have joined together, as is (well-)
known.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

As Geldner says, the subject here probably remains the Maruts. The question is whether тАЬwhich is in heavenтАЭ is a restrictive or non-restrictive relative clause - that is, are there various possible tracks and itтАЩs the one in heaven that they like, or is there one track and it happens to be in heaven. My inclination is to take it as restrictive, and the track or footstep in which they take pleasure is the one called elsewhere the param├б- (I.22.20-21, 72.2, 4, 154.5, etc.), upam├б- (V.3.3), or uttam├б- (V.51.4) тАШhighestтАЩ, as well as div├бs pad├б- (IX.10.9, 83.2). There seems to be an implicit contrast to this high and distant pad├б-, which they like, and тАЬthe navel of the sacrificeтАЭ (n─Б╠Бbh─Б yaj├▒├бsya), where they find themselves. But these locations may be more complementary than contrastive, since the тАЬhighest track/footstepтАЭ often seems to indicate a place where a heavenly form of the earthly sacrifice is conducted simultaneously. See, e.g., I.22.20-21 and remarks on I.21.6.

+Griffith

These his victorious followers bold in the heavens the place they love,

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWhen the ceremony is being prepared in the hall of sacrifice, this (Indra), having inspected the rite,regulates (the performance) in due succession for a distant object.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Distant object: for future rewards; “this (Indra)for a long prospect, in the east proceeding sacrifice, measures, having considered in succession the sacrifice”,agam d─лrgh─Бya cakс╣гase pr─Бc─л prayati adhvare mim─лte yaj├▒am anuс╣гag vicakс╣гya

+Jamison Brereton

This oneтАФto take the long view while the rite is going forth toward the eastтАФ
measures the sacrifice in proper order, having surveyed it.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

This verse uses some of the material found in the previous hymn, also in Uс╣гс╣Зih: pr─Б╠Бci prayaty ├аdhvar├й is a heavy variant of pr─Б╠Бdhvar├й (that is, pr├б adhvar├й) of VIII.12.31-33; m├нm─лte is identical to the refrain m├нm─лta ├нd (12.10-12); ─Бnuс╣г├бk occurs in 12.11.

Who is ay├бm? This near demonstrative should mean that the referent is actually present. It can only be Indra. In the first two verses of the tс╣Ыca the focus is on his companions, the Maruts (тАЬwho are yours [=Indra]тАЭ 28a), and now attention turns to their leader, the subject of the hymn as a whole, and in the finale to the hymn his longed-for epiphany is signalled by this dramatic ay├бm.

That Indra himself тАЬmeasures the sacrificeтАЭ is consistent with his being urged to тАЬstretch the threadтАЭ in 14c above.

GeldnerтАЩs interpretation of ab is quite different from mine, and seems to envisage the sacrifice receding in the distance as the subject keeps gazing further out towards it. This doesnтАЩt make much sense to me, and the similarity of the expression in b to the cliched pr├б adhvar├й (see just above), which refers to the temporal progress of the ritual (and in this case, perhaps the carrying of the ─Аhavan─лya fire eastward), makes his interpretation unlikely.

The only other occurrence of d─лrgh─Б╠Бya c├бkс╣гase is in I.7.3, where Indra puts the sun in the sky for this purpose. See remarks ad loc., where I point out that the expression can be either temporal or locational or both.

Er l├д├Яt sich lange sehen, w├дhrend das Opfer weiter vor sich geht; er mi├Яt das Opfer mit dem Blick pr├╝fend richtig ab.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe stone (that bruises the Soma) is the showerer (of benefits), so is your exhilaration and this Somathat is effused; the sacrifice that you accept is the showerer (of benefits),such also is your invocation.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Vс╣Ыс╣г─Б: isreiterated in the following с╣Ыcas; vс╣Ыс╣г─Б yam indra te ratha uto te vс╣Ыс╣гaс╣Зa havi = k─Бm─Бn─Бm varс╣гit─Б

+Jamison Brereton

A bull is the pressing stone, a bull the exhilarating drink, and a bull this pressed soma here.
A bull is the sacrifice that you urge onward, and our call is a bull.

+Griffith

Strong is the press-stone, strong thy joy, strong is the flowing Soma juice:
Strong is the rite thou furtherest, strong is our call.

+Geldner

Bullengleich ist der Pre├Яstein, bullengleich der Rausch, bullengleich dieser ausgepre├Яte Soma; bullengleich ist das Opfer, zu dem du kommst, bullengleich der Ruf nach dir.

+Grassmann

Ein Stier der Stein, ein Stier der Trank, ein Stier der Soma, hier gepresst, Ein Stier das Opfer, das du hegst, ein Stier der Ruf.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe showerer (of the oblation) I invoke with manifold and gratifying (praises) you, O thunderer, theshowerer (of benefits); inasmuch as you acknowledge the eulogy addressed to you, your invocation is theshowerer (of benefits).тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

As a bull, I call upon you, the bull, o mace-bearer, together with your brilliant help,
for you cherish a responsive praise, and our call is a bull.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

pr├бtiс╣гс╣нuti- occurs only here. I assume that it is a praise-hymn made in response to whatever the god has done for us, though Geldner suggests it is a praise that corresponds to IndraтАЩs greatness.

+Griffith

As strong I call on thee the Strong, O Thunderer with thy thousand aids:
For thou hast won the hymn of praise. Strong is our call.

+Geldner

Als Bulle lade ich dich, den Bullen, o Keulentr├дger, samt deinen wunderbaren Hilfen, denn du hast auf das entsprechende Lob Anspruch. Bullengleich ist der Ruf nach dir.

+Grassmann

Ich rufe dich, der Stier den Stier, durch viele Laben, Blitzender; Denn du bist hold dem Lobgesang, ein Stier der Ruf.

+Elizarenkova
